<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6214432430541636744">When the NSA's invincible code-breaking machine encounters a mysterious code it cannot break, the agency calls its head cryptographer, Susan Fletcher, a brilliant and beautiful mathematician. What she uncovers sends shock waves through the corridors of power. The NSA is being held hostage ... not by guns or bombs, but by a code so ingeniously complex that if released it wo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6214432430541636744">When the NSA's invincible code-breaking machine encounters a mysterious code it cannot break, the agency calls its head cryptographer, Susan Fletcher, a brilliant and beautiful mathematician. What she uncovers sends shock waves through the corridors of power. The NSA is being held hostage ... not by guns or bombs, but by a code so ingeniously complex that if released it would cripple U.S. intelligence. Caught in an accelerating tempest of secrecy and lies, Susan Fletcher battles to save the agency she believes in. Betrayed on all sides, she finds herself fighting not only for her country but also for her life, and in the end, for the life of the man she loves.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_39702492">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39702492" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/668409-claus" class="left imgcol" title="Claus"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442480792p2/668409.jpg" alt="Claus" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/39702492?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 04, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/668409-claus" class="user" title="Claus">Claus</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11125.Digital_Fortress" title="Paperback 9780552151696" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/668409-claus?shelf=audio-books" class="actionLinkLite">audio-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/668409-claus?shelf=1-star" class="actionLinkLite">1-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer39702492">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6091939457815908475">It is truely mind-boggling how Dan Brown can get away with putting so many factual errors about cryptography and computers into a single book. Doesn't he have anybody proofread his manuscripts? It is also surprising that a so highly praised writer can write so badly.<br /><br />In "Digital Fortress" we enter a universe where:<br /><br />* A 64-bit code requires 64 characters to type. (Fact: 64 bits can be easily typed with 16 characters or less.)<br /><br />* Public Key Cryptography requires the exchange of a secret passkey. (Fact</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6091939457815908475">It is truely mind-boggling how Dan Brown can get away with putting so many factual errors about cryptography and computers into a single book. Doesn't he have anybody proofread his manuscripts? It is also surprising that a so highly praised writer can write so badly.<br /><br />In "Digital Fortress" we enter a universe where:<br /><br />* A 64-bit code requires 64 characters to type. (Fact: 64 bits can be easily typed with 16 characters or less.)<br /><br />* Public Key Cryptography requires the exchange of a secret passkey. (Fact: One of the nice features about Public Key Cryptography is that it does NOT require the exchange of a secret passkey.)<br /><br />* The concept of an unbreakable code is an impossibility as it violates the "Bergofsky principle". (Fact: The "One-time Pad" encryption invented more than 90 years ago is unbreakable (but often unpractical to use).)<br /><br />* A password consisting of five random characters is a really good one.<br /><br />* If you hide a backdoor in an algorithm, only the author of the algorithm will be able to find it.<br /><br /><br />On a less technical side, in "Digital Fortress" we enter a universe where:<br /><br />* A German addresses a total stranger as "Du" instead of "Sie".<br /><br />* A university teacher willingly accepts a secret overseas mission for the NSA, just because the man who calls him happens to be his wife's boss.<br /><br />* A young man who appears to have lived for a few months in Spain doesn't know the difference between dollars and pesetas. (The book was written before the Euro currency was introduced.)<br /><br />* The NSA apparently have no backup of the data in their main databank.<br /><br />* Pigs actually do fly. (Okay, I didn't acturally read that, but I'm sure it must be in there somewhere.)<br /><br /><br />Add to this that the characters behave in ridiculously silly and unlikely ways. (For example, this man wants to buy a ring from a frightened, young woman. Does he say, "I would like to buy your ring"? No, he says "You have something I need; but I'll pay you for it," which of course frightens the woman even more.) Add some annoyingly long filler sentences completely lacking in content and serving only to use ink.<br /><br />Not a good book. The only reason I read it to the end was because I kept believing that it must get better eventually. It didn't. In the final crisis the book reaches new levels of bad writing: <br /><br />* The computer science is bogus.<br /><br />* The assembled scientists cannot solve this problem: "What number best expresses the difference between Uranium 238 and Uranium 235?". In the final second of the crisis, after twenty minutes of thinking, somebody suddenly, surpisingly discovers that the answer is 3. (I am not exaggerating!)<br /><br />* The writing style is an incredibly long-winded, drawn out, ink-wasting collection of superfluous words. (If the world was about to fall apart unless you discovered an important number in the next five minutes, would you spend that time pointing out to your colleagues that the word "man-made" is not a number? No, I thought not.)<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6091939457815908475">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/10654270?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 18, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/293948-seizure-romero" class="user" title="Seizure Romero">Seizure Romero</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

              <a href="/review/list/293948-seizure-romero?shelf=shite" class="actionLinkLite">shite</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/293948-seizure-romero?shelf=zzzzznrk" class="actionLinkLite">zzzzznrk</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer10654270">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13073286204541685256">There's a reason why everyone talks about The DaVinci Code and not about this book. I have no idea what that reason would be, because I thought Angels &amp; Demons was mediocre so I never bothered to read the The DaVinci Code. Anyway, I was bored and a copy of this was sitting at the library for a quarter and I thought "WTF, mate, I'll give it a go."<br /><br />The first page of chapter 1 starts with Susan Fletcher waking from a romantic dream to the ringing of the telephone:<br /><br />"Susan, it's David. Did I wake y</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13073286204541685256">There's a reason why everyone talks about The DaVinci Code and not about this book. I have no idea what that reason would be, because I thought Angels &amp; Demons was mediocre so I never bothered to read the The DaVinci Code. Anyway, I was bored and a copy of this was sitting at the library for a quarter and I thought "WTF, mate, I'll give it a go."<br /><br />The first page of chapter 1 starts with Susan Fletcher waking from a romantic dream to the ringing of the telephone:<br /><br />"Susan, it's David. Did I wake you?"<br />She smiled, rolling over in bed. "I was just dreaming of you. Come over and play."<br />He laughed. "It's still dark out."<br />"Mmm." She moaned sensuously. "Then <em>definitely</em> come over and play. We can sleep in before we head north."<br /><br />That is not a transcription typo, or the manifestation of my unfocused rage. It really does read <em>'"Mmm." She moaned sensuously.'</em> Please feel free to vomit if you need to; I'll wait.<br /><br />David then proceeds to postpone their plans to celebrate their six-month engagement due to something hush-hush, like maybe his being a big homo. C'mon, what sort of man is going to pass up some sweet, sweet lovin' before disappearing on a mystery mission? The kind who likes other men, that's what kind. A handful of pages later, it becomes clear that Dan Brown has read too many <a title="Clive Cussler" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18411.Clive_Cussler">Clive Cussler</a> novels as we're treated to a description of David Becker:<br /><br />"Becker was dark--a rugged, youthful thirty-five with sharp green eyes and a wit to match. His strong jaw and taut features reminded Susan of carved marble. Over six feet tall, Becker moved across a squash court faster than any of his colleagues could comprehend. After soundly beating his opponent, he would cool off by dousing his head in a drinking fountain and soaking his tuft of thick, black hair. Then, still dripping, he'd treat his opponent to a fruit shake and a bagel."<br /><br />Is it just me or does this read like Dan Brown was typing this with one hand? Why does Mr. Stud have the same initials as the author? Why would anyone want a sharp green wit? And is 'fruit shake' some sort of code for gay sex? Is that why he is still dripping?<br /><br />So then, after all this ran through my immature little mind, I remembered I had other books to read--books that didn't suck horrifically within the first ten pages. Yay for other books!<br /><br />Oh, and I sold it to a used book shop for a dollar, so it was worth the quarter. Yay for used book shops!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13073286204541685256">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_68942489">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68942489" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely" class="left imgcol" title="K.D. Absolutely"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1449978413p2/2156200.jpg" alt="K.D. Absolutely" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/68942489?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 29, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely" class="user" title="K.D. Absolutely">K.D. Absolutely</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to K.D. by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4076088-rimon-alania">Rimon Alania</a>
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=suspense-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=populist" class="actionLinkLite">populist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer68942489">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9117480265078397401">I work in the Information Technology field so relating to this book was easy for me. I don’t know anything about NSA (National Security Agency) and how they operate but I know stuff like encryption, algorithm, anagram, computer virus, code-breaking, etc. So, this book glued me from start to finish. My officemate has been telling me that this is his favorite Dan Brown book. He said that since I’ve read all his 4 other novels, <em>The Da Vinci Code, Angels and Demons, Deception Point</em> (all 3 stars, i.e</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9117480265078397401">I work in the Information Technology field so relating to this book was easy for me. I don’t know anything about NSA (National Security Agency) and how they operate but I know stuff like encryption, algorithm, anagram, computer virus, code-breaking, etc. So, this book glued me from start to finish. My officemate has been telling me that this is his favorite Dan Brown book. He said that since I’ve read all his 4 other novels, <em>The Da Vinci Code, Angels and Demons, Deception Point</em> (all 3 stars, i.e., I liked them!) and <em>The Lost Symbol</em> (2 stars, i.e., It’s okay!) and I am glad that I finally read this book. Hurray, I am now a Dan Brown completist! <br /><br />I liked the story. NSA has a program that can track personal conversations around the world. One employee gets angry so he becomes a whistleblower. NSA hires a pretty detective (not yet Robert Langdon since this is Dan Brown’s first novel) and she is so hot most of the male characters in this book lust for her. This lust for her body and for power (as usual) basically becomes the driving force for all these men to outwit or kill each other or even themselves. The plot is a little overpopulated by characters and the twists are a bit too many to become coincidental. However, this is Dan Brown’s first novel so they are expected. Just like any other first time novelists, Brown was trying to prove that he could intricately weave a suspenseful yet unbelievable plot.<br /><br />Wikipedia says that this book was based on real-life incident in cryptography. The story seems to tell me that Dan Brown not only did his thorough research on the topic but was also able to anticipate what NSA would do. He was a step ahead of NSA or maybe the NSA was influenced by the book. This one was not coincidence, I think. Or maybe Dan Brown was clever enough to befriend an insider in NSA. I just did not have any idea how a novelist could have access to NSA. Or maybe I am reading too many suspense-thriller books (Robert Ludlum, Jeffrey Archer, Ken Follett, John Grisham, etc) that my rational thinking is now tainted with all these far-fetched possibilities or thoughts.<br /><br />Dan Brown was born on the same year I was, i.e., 1964. His books have been translated in many languages and stayed in New York’s Bestsellers’ List and adapted into big movie blockbusters. Wimps cannot do just those. I like Dan Brown definitely not for his literary prowess, i.e., his writing is ordinary, but for his imagination and the efforts that he put in his research. He just does not sit down and types away his thoughts. He backs those up with facts. He goes to the museums in Paris or Capital Building, looks up on all the writings or symbols on the wall, paintings, towers. He reads history and current events and incorporates those to his plot. So, let’s spare this guy from our senseless tirades. We just cannot ignore the fact that he knows his trade. His books deserve to be read. His efforts deserve to be appreciated. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9117480265078397401">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_7577338">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7577338" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/169863-lydia" class="left imgcol" title="Lydia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1188175431p2/169863.jpg" alt="Lydia" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/7577338?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 12, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/169863-lydia" class="user" title="Lydia">Lydia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11125.Digital_Fortress" title="Paperback 9780552151696" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/169863-lydia?shelf=partially-read" class="actionLinkLite">partially-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/169863-lydia?shelf=partiallyread" class="actionLinkLite">partiallyread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer7577338">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16454596311908730093">When I first read the DaVinci Code a couple of years back, I admit that it wasn't all that bad (at least for the first two-thirds or so), but in light of its content I found it significantly overrated... Upon reading this book, however, I am outright insulted that this man's success is inspiring documentaries on the History Channel...<br /><br />I had the unfortunate luck to inherit this along with a box of other (and thankfully much more redeeming) books when a good friend of mine was leaving Japan. After</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16454596311908730093">When I first read the DaVinci Code a couple of years back, I admit that it wasn't all that bad (at least for the first two-thirds or so), but in light of its content I found it significantly overrated... Upon reading this book, however, I am outright insulted that this man's success is inspiring documentaries on the History Channel...<br /><br />I had the unfortunate luck to inherit this along with a box of other (and thankfully much more redeeming) books when a good friend of mine was leaving Japan. After getting about ten pages into it, I found myself almost in tears laughing at the downright, blatant lack of knowledge that Dan Brown has regarding central themes to his novel, namely languages, national intelligence, and... intelligence in the traditional sense. Brown's affected knowledge of, well, /anything/ in this so-called book is almost as equal in transparency as is the pretentious description of the lead male character:<br /><br />"David Becker. The only man she’d ever loved. The youngest full professor at Georgetown University and a brilliant foreign-language specialist, he was practically a celebrity in the world of academia. Born with an eidetic memory and a love of languages, he’d mastered six Asian dialects as well as Spanish, French, and Italian."<br /><br />Wow, Dan Brown outdoes himself. Not only has he managed to create an over-the-top Professor Superman in tennis shorts (complete with a sexy uber-genius side-chick to fawn over him), Brown has also successfully condensed all the languages of an entire continent into one, vast, super language called Asian, of which said Professor can speak... six dialects!<br /><br />"His university lectures on etymology and linguistics were standing-room only, and he invariably stayed late to answer a barrage of questions. He spoke with authority and enthusiasm, apparently oblivious to the adoring gazes of his star-struck coeds. Becker was dark—a rugged, youthful thirty-five with sharp green eyes and a wit to match. His strong jaw and taut features reminded Susan of carved marble. Over six feet tall, Becker moved across a squash court faster than..." <br /><br />Puke. I rate this book a one, despite not even having had the will to get through the first quarter of it, as my brain was threatening to stuff itself down my throat and asphyxiate me if I continued to subject it to such garbage.<br /><br />And before you get all indignant on me, know this: Under normal circumstances, I wouldn't be put out of my way to knock a book so hard. I would simply toss it aside like all the other trash pulp fiction out there in the airport bookstores and never think of it again. But yet, America, you are snatching up millions of copies of this man's books, singing his praises, and casting A-list stars in big-screen productions of his non-original, factually inaccurate trash. Please, stop it. You're scaring me.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16454596311908730093">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class="brown_comment" id="comment_85726958">
  <div class="xhr_comment_photo">
    	<a href="/user/show/169863-lydia" alt="Lydia"><img alt="169863" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1188175431p1/169863.jpg" /></a>
  </div>
  <div class="xhr_comment_body">
    <a href="/user/show/169863-lydia" style="font-weight:bold">Lydia</a>

      
<span id="freeTextContainer8824348573506732406">Joseph, you are certainly correct that the cutoff between a dialect and a language can be vague in many cases, and you have a point about different ty</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8824348573506732406">Joseph, you are certainly correct that the cutoff between a dialect and a language can be vague in many cases, and you have a point about different types of Chinese (which are not mutually intelligible) being classified as the same "language." However, in this case, one of these so-called "dialects" that the protagonist speaks is Japanese. As someone who has lived in Japan for over a decade, has a M.A. In Japanese to English translation and five-years' experience working in the field of applied linguistics, I can assure you that it is not accurate to refer to the Japanese language (which itself subsumes a wide range of dialects, some of which can not be understood by other native speakers) as an "Asian dialect." <br /><br />Perhaps my harsh attitude against this book stems from the fact that it treads on my area of expertise, but then again, I'm sure that historians and theologians felt similarly about /The Da Vinci Code/. Moreover, I do not believe that one has to be much of an expert on any of these subjects to see through Brown's feigned competence, which perhaps illustrates well why I personally believe that authors should follow the adage "write what you know." <br /><br />But then again, if it sells books, more power to him. I stand by my criticisms, though, in that I think he is not worthy of the praise that he has received, and I am more ashamed of the hype the public has given Brown than I am critical of Brown himself.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8824348573506732406">...more</a>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer28286233">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10916573626843043950">I learned that Dan Brown is a bad writer and I will never read any of his other books. I also am upset at my friend for recommending me this book.<br /><p><br />In short, the book is a bad novel, and a very bad novel if you know anything about math / cryptography.<br />Not only the technical errors were appalling, but the writing style itself is mediocre.<br /></p><p><br /><strong>WARNING: spoiler here.</strong><br /><br />There is a scene where the heads of NSA along with some of the smartest people on Earth were trying to solve a riddle left by the bad guy as a</p></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10916573626843043950">I learned that Dan Brown is a bad writer and I will never read any of his other books. I also am upset at my friend for recommending me this book.<br /><p><br />In short, the book is a bad novel, and a very bad novel if you know anything about math / cryptography.<br />Not only the technical errors were appalling, but the writing style itself is mediocre.<br /></p><p><br /><strong>WARNING: spoiler here.</strong><br /><br />There is a scene where the heads of NSA along with some of the smartest people on Earth were trying to solve a riddle left by the bad guy as a clue. It took them a whole chapter to solve the riddle, these people who with IQ of supposedly 170+. But I, a reader with average IQ and no formal training in cryptography, knew instantly what the riddle is all about. How is that realistic? either Dan Brown's IQ is below average, or it doesn't take that much to become the head of NSA. I opt for the former.<br /></p><p><br />The character development is weak, no strong plot lines, and the dialogs were so bad they could have been written by me. Total waste of time. The only fun I got from this book was the time I wrote this review to bash it.</p></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_330177035">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/330177035" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4428084-kim" class="left imgcol" title="Kim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1324875620p2/4428084.jpg" alt="Kim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/330177035?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 04, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4428084-kim" class="user" title="Kim">Kim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11125.Digital_Fortress" title="Paperback 9780552151696" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4428084-kim?shelf=of-heroines-and-heroin-books" class="actionLinkLite">of-heroines-and-heroin-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4428084-kim?shelf=made-me-think" class="actionLinkLite">made-me-think</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer330177035">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8683419190037460812">I'm not sure what to believe after reading this book. I've always liked Dan Brown's books because he writes so realistically, using big words to belittle readers about how little they know.<br />Or so I thought.<br />After reading this book, I did a little snooping of my own (OK, those were big words too, I just used Google) and realised that most of the technology, computers and cool machinery did not exist. In fact, Goodreads was an excellent source of information of unhappy reviewers tearing down this bo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8683419190037460812">I'm not sure what to believe after reading this book. I've always liked Dan Brown's books because he writes so realistically, using big words to belittle readers about how little they know.<br />Or so I thought.<br />After reading this book, I did a little snooping of my own (OK, those were big words too, I just used Google) and realised that most of the technology, computers and cool machinery did not exist. In fact, Goodreads was an excellent source of information of unhappy reviewers tearing down this book's credibility. Gee, I was really hoping that those stuff were as cool as mentioned in Digital Fortress.<br />But that asides, there are some historical facts and figures that ARE real, if not as cool. NSA. Cryptology. Enigma. Although I can't say that Brown's books are an excellent crash course for a myriad of whacky subjects, his writings definitely introduced readers to an entirely whole new world that most of us would have otherwise never have dreamt about.<br />Having that said, I can't say that Brown's writing style is my favourite. His books usually start off well, but kind of go downhill somewhat at the end. His plot developments are not the best I've come across, although how he comes up with them in the bloody first place is unthinkable. But I must say, there is a significant similarity between the plots in most, if not all, of his books. It doesn't take a cryptologist to figure it out. Now before this I've only read 3 of his books (OK that may be quite a lot already) and my recent awareness of such similarity has indeed taken out most surprises within Brown's novels.<br />No spoiler here, though I'm sure most of us can tell what it is by now. I would still recommend Dan Brown's books any day, despite the slight low ratings on Goodreads. I am aware that most readers claim that Brown has twisted reality to the most atrocious of levels. Thankfully, for a person with <em>no clue</em> about any of the topics he's ever written about so far, I have no problem with enjoying the book at all. But I'm sure that if Dan Brown were to write about something I was excellent at and passionate about - watching TV, Facebooking, sleeping - he'd be getting a thrashing from me as well. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8683419190037460812">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_610649310">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/610649310" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1091417-aj-leblanc" class="left imgcol" title="AJ LeBlanc"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1348666088p2/1091417.jpg" alt="AJ LeBlanc" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/610649310?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 19, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1091417-aj-leblanc" class="user" title="AJ LeBlanc">AJ LeBlanc</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1091417-aj-leblanc?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1091417-aj-leblanc?shelf=book-group-pick" class="actionLinkLite">book-group-pick</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1091417-aj-leblanc?shelf=cbr-v" class="actionLinkLite">cbr-v</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer610649310">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2085044043738395005">My book group chose this book and I will never forgive them.<br /><br />I’ve never read anything by Dan Brown. He doesn’t write my type of fiction, so while I was aware that he’s a huge success, I never bothered to pick any of his books up because I knew I wouldn’t be interested.<br /><br />What I didn’t know is how much of a shit writer he is.<br /><br />I’m sure he cries into a giant pile of money every single time someone tells him that.<br /><br /><br /><br />Digital Fortress is about the government and secrecy. Susan Fletcher works for a super top s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2085044043738395005">My book group chose this book and I will never forgive them.<br /><br />I’ve never read anything by Dan Brown. He doesn’t write my type of fiction, so while I was aware that he’s a huge success, I never bothered to pick any of his books up because I knew I wouldn’t be interested.<br /><br />What I didn’t know is how much of a shit writer he is.<br /><br />I’m sure he cries into a giant pile of money every single time someone tells him that.<br /><br /><br /><br />Digital Fortress is about the government and secrecy. Susan Fletcher works for a super top secret government agency called NSA that cracks codes to read emails and save the world. How do I remember that her name is Susan Fletcher? Susan Fletcher is referred to as Susan Fletcher on every page that Susan Fletcher appears on. Apparently Brown is worried that people won’t remember that Susan Fletcher is one of the main character is his book Digital Fortress by Dan Brown.<br /><br />Susan Fletcher is the best code breaker NSA has. Susan Fletcher is also beautiful and perfect and everyone loves her and wants to do her. Susan Fletcher has a brilliant mind. Susan Fletcher is also very attractive. Susan Fletcher is also smart. People look at Susan Fletcher and think to themselves “How does an IQ of 170 fit into a body that attractive? I am going to think more of these thoughts so that the reader of Dan Brown’s Digital Fortress will know what Susan Fletcher looks like in the book Digital Fortress by Dan Brown.”<br /><br />Your first drinking game is to take a shot every time someone chuckles.<br /><br />Your next drinking game is to empty a Red Solo Cup every time someone’s eyes are described as strong hazel, deep green, inky black, sable, gray, or any other color that barely exists in real life. Yes, people do have these eyes, and apparently they all live in Dan Brown’s world. Dan Brown wrote the book Digital Fortress.<br /><br />If you do not drink and are into health, do push ups or squats or something instead of pounding booze. Either way, we’re all going to crumple to the floor and throw up.<br /><br />When Susan Fletcher is called in to work on a Saturday by Commander Strathmore, head of NSA, Susan Fletcher knows that something must be very wrong. Susan Fletcher was supposed to be on a vacation with her finance David Becker. David Becker is beautiful and smart. David Becker plays squash and no one minds when David Becker puts his entire head into the water fountain to wash away the sweat. David Becker is that amazing.<br /><br />Turns out that the Commander has sent David Becker, Susan Fletcher’s finance, to Spain, even though David Becker does not work for NSA. Susan Fletcher thinks thoughts to tell the reader how important NSA is.<br /><br /><br />Seriously, how is this guy a big name writer? I just don’t get it.<br />Dan Brown, the author of Digital Fortress, does not have time for important things like “Show, don’t tell.” when it comes to writing his books. Dan Brown wants to get to the important things like telling the reader how intelligent and beautiful Susan Fletcher and David Becker are. Susan Fletcher and David Becker are engaged. Susan Fletcher and David Becker have been engaged for six months. Susan Fletcher tells David Becker this when she says “You do remember we’re engaged, don’t you?” which is exactly what people in real life would say if they wanted to let you know that they were engaged.<br /><br />Susan Fetcher stays underground in the NSA bunker trying to figure out what is wrong with their giant, enormous, massive, expensive, costly, top secret, classified translator project. The computer is used to cull through email and crack codes and save the entire planet. It has done so successfully. But now it has found a code that it cannot crack and Susan Fletcher has to use her beautiful body and intelligent mind to solve the problem.<br /><br />Meanwhile, in Spain, David Becker is on a crazy journey of his own. He has to find a ring because it somehow has something to do with this code. He is able to follow thin clues to track the ring from person to person. Apparently David Becker, with no training (because if he had training, someone in the book Digital Fortress by Dan Brown, would have told us about it) becomes the world’s most brilliant detective. Oh, and also David Becker is given stupid coincidences that tell him where to go next. David Becker is smart and is able to use these giant arrows to find the next person to talk to.<br /><br />Of course everything turns out to be suspicious and there’s lots of traitors and threats from every side. One thing I did like about the book Digital Fortress, written by Dan Brown, is that there were parts where I honestly didn’t know who the bad guy was. Luckily Dan Brown quickly tells information to make me pay attention to a specific character in his book Digital Fortress and I, the reader, can get back to the important part which is remembering that Susan Fletcher and David Becker are engaged and they are both very intelligent and very beautiful.<br /><br />The crazy ending was kind of fun because everyone was in the same place sort of screaming and trying to solve the problem before the entire government was shut down, but other than that… What the fuck, America? This is one of our top selling authors?<br /><br />In conclusion, I did not like the book Digital Fortress by Dan Brown. Not only do I not care for this type of story, I could not get past the writing. How does this happen?<br /><br />I don’t care if this makes me sound like a book snob, but seriously, this is who we’ve chosen as one of our Must Read Authors? For fuck’s sake.<br /><br />My book group meets tomorrow and I’m bringing a giant list of discussion questions. Apparently they all hated the book too, <strong>including the two people who suggested it for this month</strong>. Way to make the rest of us pay for your mistakes.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2085044043738395005">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6485031428176720744">No matter what people want to say about Dan Brown or his books or hatred towards him you got to admire the fact that what he brings to the table no one else does.<br /><br />This was the book which brought me to the beautiful world of books.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText6485031428176720744">No matter what people want to say about Dan Brown or his books or hatred towards him you got to admire the fact that what he brings to the table no one else does.<br /><br />This was the book which brought me to the beautiful world of books. Before reading this book I though reading was a bit cissy and a waste of time since everything is fictional, why not better read some spiritual/self help and knowledge books. After reading this book everything changed, I started to read more and more fiction and today books have become one of the most important parts of my life all thanks to this books.<br /><br />Today I have read all of Dan Brown books apart from Angels &amp; Demons but this book remains to be my favorite. I agree that he is not a great writer and uses the same formula in every of his books, not versatile at all.   <a href="/user/show/1499461-samuel" class="left imgcol" title="Samuel"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1224430732p2/1499461.jpg" alt="Samuel" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/45964620?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 17, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1499461-samuel" class="user" title="Samuel">Samuel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11125.Digital_Fortress" title="Paperback 9780552151696" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer45964620">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14680642555280139112">What would happen if every nation and person in the would, with a computer, could access every top secret file of the government? This is what Susan Fletcher and David Becker have to prevent in Digital Fortress by Dan Brown. With a lot of action and suspense Digital Fortress is a book for anyone who likes action.<br /><br />Dan Brown wrote many other action novels. I have read all of them and this novel is just as good of a read as the rest. This novel is written in the same style as all the others. Leaving</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14680642555280139112">What would happen if every nation and person in the would, with a computer, could access every top secret file of the government? This is what Susan Fletcher and David Becker have to prevent in Digital Fortress by Dan Brown. With a lot of action and suspense Digital Fortress is a book for anyone who likes action.<br /><br />Dan Brown wrote many other action novels. I have read all of them and this novel is just as good of a read as the rest. This novel is written in the same style as all the others. Leaving in the suspense in all his books, Dan Brown makes all his novels an exiting read.<br /><br />The United States government has just bought a huge computer that can unscramble any code called TRANSLTR. A top secret government agency called National Security Agency, NSA, has purchased this computer to prevent terrorist from sending coded messages to other terrorist inside or out of the United States. Thinking the people of the US may considerTRANSLTR a breech of privacy, the government never told any one about the device.<br /><br />Susan Fletcher is the head Cryptographer at the NSA Crypto facility. David Becker is a foreign-language specialist Georgetown University. Commander Greg Strathmore is in charge of the facility. There also are three other Cryptographers and many engineers who work on TRANSLTR in the facility.<br /><br />Susan Fletcher head Cryptographer notices a code that TRANSLTR has been working on for Eighteen hours, and most files take less than one hour. A few days latter a strange address sends them an email. Sending the email, let the NSA figure up a way to shut down Digital Fortress. The virus that will shut downTRANSLTER and expose the main government data bank to any one with Internet access. Exposing the data bank, will put the nation at risk of attack and total chaos of the citizens.<br /><br />The NSA sends in David Becker to receive the ring that has the code to shut down Digital Fortress. In the mean time, Susan Fletcher is trying to convince the head boss of the whole operation that there is a problem. David is nearly shot to death, and Susan is nearly blown to bits. Will the two succeed?<br /><br />I would recommend this book to anyone. This book has got a lot of action, and is a story that leaves you wandering, what if. However, if you have a little bit of a soft stomach this novel will leave you wanting to turn away at times. This book is for any one who likes to left on the edge of there seat for the whole story, till the end.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14680642555280139112">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_6933002">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6933002" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/425220-lissa" class="left imgcol" title="Lissa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451785597p2/425220.jpg" alt="Lissa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/6933002?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 04, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/425220-lissa" class="user" title="Lissa">Lissa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11125.Digital_Fortress" title="Paperback 9780552151696" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer6933002">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12132220737396152246">Oh Dan Brown, how I love to hate you. It seems a universal truth that when you have run out of all of the books to read that you’ve brought with you, it is impossible to find decent reading material wherever you are. <br /><br />Shamefully, I’ve actually read most of his books. I read Angels and Demons because someone recommended it to me. Though I found his writing to be extraordinarily poor, I found the story to be engaging enough to overlook that fact. I didn’t guess the ending, and it posited some fasci</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12132220737396152246">Oh Dan Brown, how I love to hate you. It seems a universal truth that when you have run out of all of the books to read that you’ve brought with you, it is impossible to find decent reading material wherever you are. <br /><br />Shamefully, I’ve actually read most of his books. I read Angels and Demons because someone recommended it to me. Though I found his writing to be extraordinarily poor, I found the story to be engaging enough to overlook that fact. I didn’t guess the ending, and it posited some fascinating ideas about history. I read The DaVinici Code because everyone was reading it and because I liked Angels and Demons. The DaVinici Code was written equally poorly, but I noticed a lot of similarities in the plots of the two novels. But it was still an entertaining read so I figured I’d forgive it. Then, on my way to Costa Rica, I realized that I didn’t bring enough books with me for the plan ride. I went to the bookstore in Charlotte, North Carolina and picked up Deception Point, yet another Dan Brown masterpiece. The plot of this book was “The DaVinci Code Goes Arctic”. That’s when I realized that Dan Brown came up with one good plot and he’s just recycling it over and over again.<br /><br />Even so, faced with the prospect of Rich Dad, Poor Dad or He’s Just Not In To You, I picked up Digital Fortress. I do think his writing is getting better, but I had the ending of the book figured out within the first ten pages. I didn’t even have to read the ending first to know what was going to happen. Maybe I’ll register Digital Fortress on bookcrossing and send it out into the world.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12132220737396152246">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_5826343">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5826343" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/355666-dan" class="left imgcol" title="Dan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442474229p2/355666.jpg" alt="Dan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/5826343?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 07, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/355666-dan" class="user" title="Dan">Dan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11125.Digital_Fortress" title="Paperback 9780552151696" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">beach read</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/355666-dan?shelf=thrillers" class="actionLinkLite">thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer5826343">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1083643014480649164">Here’s the problem: Digital Fortress has a good plot, but it’s filled with weak characters. I really liked the plot. A disgruntled NSA employee develops an unbreakable encryption program (the Digital Fortress) and threatens to give both the encryption program and the key (which is buried in the program) away on the Internet. If the bad guys gain access to the key, they will be able to communicate without fear of the NSA decrypting their messages. This throws the NSA into a panic – as it should –</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1083643014480649164">Here’s the problem: Digital Fortress has a good plot, but it’s filled with weak characters. I really liked the plot. A disgruntled NSA employee develops an unbreakable encryption program (the Digital Fortress) and threatens to give both the encryption program and the key (which is buried in the program) away on the Internet. If the bad guys gain access to the key, they will be able to communicate without fear of the NSA decrypting their messages. This throws the NSA into a panic – as it should – so they send David Becker to track down the former employee. However, David learns that the man has died in suspicious circumstances, so … well, you know. <br /><br />Pretty good so far, but now consider the main characters. Susan Fletcher and David Becker are the perfect pair. She’s beautiful, intelligent, sexy and decent to the core. He’s beautiful, intelligent, sexy and – yes – decent to the core. Although Susan has an IQ of 170, she’s mostly eye candy. The only surprise was that nobody tied her to railroad tracks in front of an oncoming train. Although that might have improved her characterization. David, on the other hand turns out to be the greatest daredevil of all time, outwitting a professional assassin, even though the most exciting thing he has done is to thrash an opponent on a squash court (and then treat him to a fruit shake and bagel). There’s another character known only as Jabba … enough said? <br /><br /> Okay, so what’s the bottom line? This clearly isn’t a top-level thriller, but if your plans fall through some weekend, this wouldn’t be a bad book to pick up. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1083643014480649164">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_998296020">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/998296020" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/9615245-arwen56" class="left imgcol" title="Arwen56"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452114932p2/9615245.jpg" alt="Arwen56" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/998296020?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 15, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9615245-arwen56" class="user" title="Arwen56">Arwen56</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/836555.Crypto" title="Hardcover 9788804559870" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/9615245-arwen56?shelf=romanzi" class="actionLinkLite">romanzi</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9615245-arwen56?shelf=lett-americana" class="actionLinkLite">lett-americana</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9615245-arwen56?shelf=usa" class="actionLinkLite">usa</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer998296020">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14467190315217499086"><br /><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/72750.gif" /><br /><br />Avevo ragione a pensare che leggendo che questo libro mi sarei fatta due sane risate. Infatti, a mio modesto avviso, Dan Brown è uno scrittore umoristico travestito da autore di <em>thriller</em>.<br /><br />A dire il vero, di risate me ne sono fatta ben più di due, perché i protagonisti hanno un “culo” che neanche i miracolati di Lourdes possono vantare. Sempre sull’orlo di un baratro, ne escono fuori illesi in virtù non tanto del loro presunto altissimo quoziente intellettivo, che in realtà deve essere assai pross</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14467190315217499086"><br /><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/72750.gif" /><br /><br />Avevo ragione a pensare che leggendo che questo libro mi sarei fatta due sane risate. Infatti, a mio modesto avviso, Dan Brown è uno scrittore umoristico travestito da autore di <em>thriller</em>.<br /><br />A dire il vero, di risate me ne sono fatta ben più di due, perché i protagonisti hanno un “culo” che neanche i miracolati di Lourdes possono vantare. Sempre sull’orlo di un baratro, ne escono fuori illesi in virtù non tanto del loro presunto altissimo quoziente intellettivo, che in realtà deve essere assai prossimo allo zero date le cretinate che fanno, quanto delle inverosimili coincidenze “casuali”. Nei romanzi di Dan Brown, infatti, il “caso” è sempre e rigorosamente dalla parte dei buoni e non gliene frega una cippa lippa di apparire esageratamente tendenzioso. No, lui no. Lui ha un compito preciso: essere l’angelo custode di quei cretini che si ostinano a mettersi nei guai. Stanno cercando un ago in un pagliaio? Lo troveranno. Stanno per cadere da un palazzo di trenta piani e sono appesi al davanzale di una finestra solo con il dito mignolo della mano sinistra? Qualcuno passerà di lì e li tirerà su. Un killer spietato che non ha mai sbagliato mira in vita sua li insegue? Non azzeccherà un colpo neanche a piangere. Stanno cercando un imprescindibile codice di accesso? Andranno su Internet, digiteranno la domanda e riceveranno la risposta. <br />Per una qualche oscura ragione, il “caso” di Dan Brown aspira a un riconoscimento ufficiale della sua costante quanto inutile bravura. Probabilmente ha un super-ego molto esigente, che non gli concede tregua, poveretto.<br /><br />Tirando le somme, dunque, come <em>thriller</em>, quale pretende di essere, la valutazione è di una stelletta (mezza sarebbe più adeguata, ma non si può, perché non c’è). Ma come romanzo comico le cinque stelle non gliele toglie nessuno. ;-)<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14467190315217499086">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/905705-caela-harrison" class="user" title="Caela Harrison">Caela Harrison</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11125.Digital_Fortress" title="Paperback 9780552151696" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer15561833">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2533968439753051106">Reading Dan Brown books is a bit like watching porn. Mildly enjoyable at the time, but not really something you'd like your friends or family to know about.<br /><br />Digital Fortress starts as it means to go on, with two-dimensional characters in a whirlwind of mystery and action. The cast never evolves beyond cardboard cut-out level, but the plot does pick up through various levels of incredulity and intrigue to a climax that ends up shallow and disappointing, leaving the reader feeling cheap and cheated</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2533968439753051106">Reading Dan Brown books is a bit like watching porn. Mildly enjoyable at the time, but not really something you'd like your friends or family to know about.<br /><br />Digital Fortress starts as it means to go on, with two-dimensional characters in a whirlwind of mystery and action. The cast never evolves beyond cardboard cut-out level, but the plot does pick up through various levels of incredulity and intrigue to a climax that ends up shallow and disappointing, leaving the reader feeling cheap and cheated.<br /><br />I understand <em>why</em> Brown is popular - the cookie-cutter formula, the "intelligent" yet criminally dim hero, the assasin and the "good guy turned mortal enemy" recipe is appealing to the masses - but can't help feeling that these books should be kept hidden on the top shelf, away from prying eyes and impressionable minds.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2533968439753051106">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_270944356">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270944356" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7590340-stefan-yates" class="left imgcol" title="Stefan Yates"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1328116275p2/7590340.jpg" alt="Stefan Yates" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/270944356?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 16, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7590340-stefan-yates" class="user" title="Stefan Yates">Stefan Yates</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7590340-stefan-yates?shelf=general-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer270944356">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7932326346401250485">Based upon how very little I'd heard about Dan Brown's two non-Robert Langdon books, I went into this one with very low expectations. However, Digital Fortress is a fairly well-written and entertaining novel. The main storyline is based upon a hush-hush operation within the NSA to obtain and or destroy the only existing copies of a pass-key that, if made public, could enable the use of an encryption program that would create coded messages that would be entirely unbreakable thereby rendering the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7932326346401250485">Based upon how very little I'd heard about Dan Brown's two non-Robert Langdon books, I went into this one with very low expectations. However, Digital Fortress is a fairly well-written and entertaining novel. The main storyline is based upon a hush-hush operation within the NSA to obtain and or destroy the only existing copies of a pass-key that, if made public, could enable the use of an encryption program that would create coded messages that would be entirely unbreakable thereby rendering the NSA obsolete and allowing undecipherable communications between terrorist organizations and crime rings throughout the world. The storyline takes place mainly in two separate locations: the top two members of the encryption team trying to break the program and track down the pass-key from headquarters and in Spain where the search is on for any possible physical pass-key possessed by the recently deceased creator of the program.<br /><br />This is a pretty fast-paced novel with lots of action on both fronts. As usual with a Dan Brown novel, things get a bit unbelievable at times, but that's part of what makes them fun. He has created an interesting cast of characters and circumstances that really keep the storyline moving along at his usual break-neck pace. I had fun reading Digital Fortress and would recommend it to fans of Mr. Browns other works and also to those who enjoy thrillers along the lines of James Patterson if you haven't yet read any of Dan Brown's other works.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7932326346401250485">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer453646057994012162">I also very much enjoyed the book and agree about how the book was very fast paced while nearing the end. One aspect of this book that I liked was tha</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText453646057994012162">I also very much enjoyed the book and agree about how the book was very fast paced while nearing the end. One aspect of this book that I liked was that the point of view kept changing throughout the course of the book. One chapter will be about Susan trying to crack the code and the next will be David’s adventurous search for the ring. Brown makes you want to keep reading by leaving cliff hangers at the ends of chapters but then switching story lines. <br />Brown also captivates the reader by making the action/ fight scenes very exciting. Chapter 100 where Hulohut, the assassin attempts to finally kill David (Brown 303) was the most intense for me. I felt it was very well written. I couldn’t stop reading. The suspense built up until BAM plot twist David has vanished! The point of view then shifts to David’s and you realize what has happened. Then the suspense builds up again. Overall, it was a great story and I feel it was executed pretty well.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_36329403">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36329403" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1642548-neal-p" class="left imgcol" title="Neal P"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1224708566p2/1642548.jpg" alt="Neal P" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/36329403?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 27, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1642548-neal-p" class="user" title="Neal P">Neal P</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11125.Digital_Fortress" title="Paperback 9780552151696" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer36329403">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17267439243978156409">Digital Fortress is a mysterious, intriguing book by Dan Brown. Dan Brown is a widely known author, who has written The Da Vinci Code and Angels and Demons. This book is about a woman named Susan Fletcher, who works for the National Security Agency (NSA). After five years of work, the NSA invented the TRANSLTR, which could break any code known to man. TRANSLTR is faced with a code that it cannot break, and when the NSA calls it head cryptographer, Susan Fletcher, she uncovers that the NSA is bei</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17267439243978156409">Digital Fortress is a mysterious, intriguing book by Dan Brown. Dan Brown is a widely known author, who has written The Da Vinci Code and Angels and Demons. This book is about a woman named Susan Fletcher, who works for the National Security Agency (NSA). After five years of work, the NSA invented the TRANSLTR, which could break any code known to man. TRANSLTR is faced with a code that it cannot break, and when the NSA calls it head cryptographer, Susan Fletcher, she uncovers that the NSA is being held hostage by a code that could cripple the U.S. intelligence. Fletcher has to find out how to break the code, while her fiancé, David Becker, is in Seville, Spain to find the man who created this code and get the pass key to break the code.<br />	Digital Fortress was one of the most fascinating novels I have read. This book had three or four different stories going on at the same time, which alternate by chapter. As you finish each chapter, the reader is always “hungry for more.” All the stories come together at the end, so you are not completely satisfied until the book is finished. Mystery books are without doubt my favorite books, but I love mystery with some kind of twist. Near the end when Fletcher is trying to break the code, Brown adds in a little science and history. He includes the isotopes of the element uranium and the system of codes that Julius Caesar used.<br />	Yet there were a few things I thought about this book that could have been improved. Having four different stories going on and then combining them at the end is a great idea, but with the fine details Dan Brown puts into each sentence it can hard to understand everything. The other thing that was a little upsetting was the end. Finding the password that would kill the virus took a series of complicated steps, but the password ended up being the number 3. I would’ve liked to see something a little more complex.<br />	Even though Digital Fortress had some bad points, it was an exciting novel that I enjoyed. Any reader who loves mysteries would love this book. Alone this book is enjoyable, but the science and the history that are mixed into the plot makes this book a techno-thriller. Even if you are not a mystery fan, it is guaranteed that this book would be fascinating to read. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17267439243978156409">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_111161337">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111161337" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3283584-bex" class="left imgcol" title="(´*•.¸?Bex?¸.•*´)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1400147426p2/3283584.jpg" alt="(´*•.¸?Bex?¸.•*´)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/111161337?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 11, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3283584-bex" class="user" title="(´*•.¸?Bex?¸.•*´)">(´*•.¸?Bex?¸.•*´)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11125.Digital_Fortress" title="Paperback 9780552151696" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3283584-bex?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer111161337">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8309473663395114479">Dan Brown has made his mark in the world of fiction by combining complex mental puzzles with action-filled adventure and romance. His thriller, "Digital Fortress" has all of these elements, and it is an exhilarating novel that raises timely and thought-provoking questions. <br /><br />A covert agency, known as NSA (jokingly, "No Such Agency"), has a multi-billion dollar secret device known as TRANSLTR that can decrypt any code. It is used to eavesdrop on encrypted email communications worldwide; the data th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8309473663395114479">Dan Brown has made his mark in the world of fiction by combining complex mental puzzles with action-filled adventure and romance. His thriller, "Digital Fortress" has all of these elements, and it is an exhilarating novel that raises timely and thought-provoking questions. <br /><br />A covert agency, known as NSA (jokingly, "No Such Agency"), has a multi-billion dollar secret device known as TRANSLTR that can decrypt any code. It is used to eavesdrop on encrypted email communications worldwide; the data that it gathers prevents terrorists from carrying out planned attacks. However, if civilians were to find out that Uncle Sam is eavesdropping on them, they might not be too pleased. Ensei Tankado, a cryptographer who was dismissed by the NSA, hates everything that TRANSTR stands for. He believes that the government has gone too far in invading people's privacy. <br /><br />Tankado claims to have created an unbreakable algorithm, known as "digital fortress," that even TRANSLTR cannot decipher. He threatens to release his algorithm unless the NSA publicly admits that it illegally gathers private information. If the general public were to learn Tankado's code, the government would lose its ability to read encrypted emails. Tankado's scheme goes awry, and what might have been merely a nuisance threatens to turn into a disaster. <br /><br />Brown makes the most of his subject. His descriptions of how cryptographers work and think are terrific, and I was fascinated by the mind-bending ciphers at the end of the novel. The protagonists, Susan Fletcher and David Becker, are nicely drawn, although a tad too superhuman. Susan is a brilliant cryptographer who works for the NSA, and David is an expert in linguistics. They both play a major role in trying to save the United States from an intelligence meltdown. <br /><br />"Digital Fortress" does have some weak points, including Brown's inability to write realistic romantic dialogue. However, when Brown sticks to sadistic assassins, wild chase scenes, and unlikely heroics, the story moves along at a breakneck pace. In addition, the author has some significant things to say about the conflict between an individual's right to privacy and the government's mission to do whatever it takes to safeguard its citizenry.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8309473663395114479">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
